### Post by hammad1337 on 2010-10-31
1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded  picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page  number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or  suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids  and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to  browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your  posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. when possible we  request that you format your posts in the following order: NOTE this is  optional

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

**Important Note:** Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be  removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image  is removed, this is why.
Same as for October...waiting for Mint 10 to release.

 Just slight changes here and there,
 I think Im just finally getting it to be exactly how I want it,

 no need to really change much. lol

### Post by TeoBigusGeekus on 2010-11-01
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> lol, grown old,
 or just reached a 'happy place'. :P

 Ive found myself not changing my desk too much in the past couple/few months either. 
 Just slight changes here and there,
 I think Im just finally getting it to be exactly how I want it,
once that happens..
 no need to really change much. lol

awhile back, there was always at least one thing that I would want to be different, but lately finding that happens less and less. lol :P

It's funny, cause sometimes I find some screenshots of my Desktop from 2 or 3 years ago buried in my hd, when I was making my first steps with linux.
It was like a circus: docks, screenlets, desklets, panels, icons, hiddeous conky scripts, etc.
Beginner's enthusiasm I guess - besides, I didn't have the knowledge to tinker with anything else than my desktop these days.
With time, I removed more and more features until I've settled down with something that suits me well.
Tinkering of course has moved to other more demanding (and dangerous) parts of my system.:P

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-01
Clicky for fullsize...
[[IMG]http://ompldr.org/vNjBheg[/IMG]]("http://ompldr.org/vNjBheQ")

Tweaking as usual. Playing with sunken menu items. Matching AWN style, semi-transparent panel. I think I'm pretty happy with this now. I half re-wrote the GTK - most widgets have their own separate text .rc file for easy editing and swapping between different styles. I've got a couple of additional menustyles, scrollbars and panel styles planned. Fixed a lot of issues. So big update tomorrow I guess... I should be asleep now.

[IMG]http://ompldr.org/vNjBiZA[/IMG]

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-02
> **koleoptero said:**
> EDIT: **@JurialMunkey**: A typo in your a new hope theme file asks for the iconset "Faenza Dark" instead of "Faenza-Dark", gnome is confused ;)

Nope, not a typo. There are two different icon sets: "Faenza-Dark" and "Faenza Dark". "Faenza Dark" is a modification of Faenza-Dark to have light rather than dark toolbar/action icons. From Here: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=132327]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=132327")


> **Rasa1111 said:**
> 
 Ive still got a couple things to figure out when I wake up,
and I might have a couple of questions for you. lol 
but this is great man,.. really great! 
Thanks! If your not using nautilus elementary, you probably want to use just normal gtk-breadcrumbs. 
Inside the "[THEME]/gtk-2.0/Styles/" directory, edit the nautilus.rc which corresponds to the theme [A-New-Hope = nautilus-dark.rc | TESB = nautilus-III.rc | ROTJ = nautilus-light.rc]. Scroll to the bottom and delete the last line which will be something along the lines of 'include "Breadcrumbs/breadcrumb-dark.rc"'. 
Save the file.
Reload the theme.
Voila! GTK style breadcrumbs.

> **-gabe-noob- said:**
> perfect perfect perfect! Your themes are boss man <333
Thanks! :D

### Post by hhh on 2010-11-02
> **Spice Weasel said:**
> Seriously, you can get the same functionality with back and forward button with the address bar and still have the ability to type out the address...
In Nautilus and Nautilus Elementary, Edit>Customize Toolbar..., drag the Edit Location pencil icon to the toolbar to switch modes. (It's also Ctrl+l to switch to location but I don't know the shortcut to switch back).

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-04
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> 
The GTK/metacity theme is here~ [http://jurialmunkey.deviantart.com/art/Divergence-IV-quot-A-New-Hope-quot-183377193?q=gallery%3Ajurialmunkey%2F18989631&qo=0](http://jurialmunkey.deviantart.com/art/Divergence-IV-quot-A-New-Hope-quot-183377193?q=gallery%3Ajurialmunkey%2F18989631&qo=0)
and the variation Im using is called  "A-new-hope-TESB".
 You will see it in the folder once you download the file. 


Hey Rasa (and other fans of A New Hope), just released an update with improved Metacity (the maximised rounding looks good now + unfocussed text is darker). Also, you will notice there is now an install script which customises the theme. No more multiple themes - just a simple Graphical script to customise the theme. Just Extract, Double click install.sh, select run and follow the dialog prompts. Doesn't even need to be run in a terminal. :D :D

> **linux18 said:**
> I spent a while getting everything just right: *snip*

And that was time well spent. Gorgeous!! :D

> 

And that was time well spent. Gorgeous!! :D

Thank you!

The wallpaper was made by me in gimp from 2 other wallpapers, 

the conky was heavily modified from one posted in the very popular UF thread, 

the Icon theme is awoken,

the dock is cairo-dock (moved just off-center to the right)

and everything is meant to blend (neutral colors, smooth gradients, etc)

I will upload the conkyrc & wallpaper once I'm done tweaking them

### Post by hammad1337 on 2010-11-05
> **cracker89 said:**
> @hammad1337 - awesoem desktop! whered u get the bar on the top?

Its conky. Here's my conkyrc:
```

alignment top-left
background no
border_width 0
cpu_avg_samples 2
default_color ffffff
color1 222222
default_outline_color black
default_shade_color black
double_buffer yes
draw_borders yes
draw_graph_borders no
draw_outline no
draw_shades no
use_xft yes
xftfont diavlo:size=14.3
xftalpha .1
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
minimum_size 1280 1024
net_avg_samples 2
double_buffer yes
out_to_console no
out_to_stderr no
extra_newline no
own_window yes
#own_window_class Conky
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
stippled_borders 0
update_interval 15.0
uppercase yes
use_spacer yes
show_graph_scale no
show_graph_range no
TEXT
${color}IT${color1}L ${color}IS${color1}ASTIME${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 35}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 15}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 20}${color}${endif}${endif}A${color1}C${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 15}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 20}${color}${endif}${endif}QUARTER${color1}DC${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 20}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 30}${color}${endif}${endif}TWENTY${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 25}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 30}${color}${endif}${else}${color1}${endif}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 5}${if_match ${exec #${color}${exec date +"%A, %d %b"}

```
I am using the Diavlo font.
My conky is stretched to cover the whole desktop, so it hides all the desktop icons.
You might want to adjust for those things in the conkyrc file.

### Post by hhh on 2010-11-05
> **koleoptero said:**
> Xfce4-notifyd in gnome?
Clever eye, it might be! Either that or an old version of notify-osd w/ no compiz running. I took a sidux xfce install and changed the sources.list to squeeze, then yanked xfce and jammed in gnome. I hadn't even fixed my screen res, but I was so surprised how well it went that I had to post a quick screen;^) Bisigi Tropical, updated notify-osd, it's coming together quickly...

[[IMG]http://img530.imageshack.us/img530/1198/screenshotokg.png[/IMG]](http://img143.imageshack.us/img143/7180/screenshotdj.png)

I need help, though. What is this taking over the volume meter???!!!...

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-06
> **koleoptero said:**
> *snip* [wallpaper]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/life1900_12.png").

EDIT: BTW your emerald themes do funky stuff when the title is larger than what the window can fit.

Thanks for the wall. Love it. Did you install the latest emerald themes. I thought I managed to fix that issue. I can't replicate it any more. In Emerald Theme Manager > Edit Themes > Titlebar "Title-bar object layout" should read: ```
(6)CNR(8)T(24)::M(4)
```

> **TroN-0074 said:**
> Why does mine looks so ugly. Please help

I think you might need to get the latest murrine engine.
In a terminal:```
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:murrine-daily/ppa
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install gtk2-engines-murrine
```

### Post by mmesantos1 on 2010-11-06
> **Mark76 said:**
> How did you get that curve in the panel as well?

Hi Mark76, 
The panels are included in the theme download, you just right click on your panel then click on properties, then click on background image radial then browse to the theme folder a choose one of the panels in the panel folder. 

I downloaded the theme from here: [http://browse.deviantart.com/?qh=&section=&q=Divergence#/d316eqx](http://browse.deviantart.com/?qh=&section=&q=Divergence#/d316eqx)

Ubuntu 8

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-11-06
> **StrayVexel said:**
> Not an Ubuntu user, but I just HAD to register when I saw this. Looks really sweet!! Has just the right amount of pop for a low contrast tiling setup yet appears very usable. One of the best. :KS

Eyedropping would make it feel like I was stealing without permission, so could you please, PLEASE paste your ~/.Xdefaults 0-15 colors? 
Also; your MOC theme looks like a custom config. Could you possibly pastebin that as well?

Loving your term prompt too. 

Thank You,
SV

:)Cheers

[[IMG]http://ompldr.org/tNjJmcg[/IMG]]("http://ompldr.org/vNjJmcg")

I've since tweaked the Xdef colours a tiny bit. Still pretty similar to the scrot your quoted.
I removed most of my app-related bits. What's here should be enough to get you the colour-scheme.
```
urxvt*font:             xft:terminus:pixelsize=8
urxvt*boldFont:         xft:terminus:pixelsize=8
urxvt*termName:         rxvt
urxvt*background:       #212629
urxvt*foreground:       #656e72
urxvt*scrollBar:        false
urxvt*matcher.button:   1
urxvt*cursorBlink:      true
urxvt*cursorColor:      #b1b6c8
urxvt*colorBD:          #857672

urxvt.transparent:      false
urxvt*allow_bold:       true

Xft*dpi:                96
Xft*antialias:          false
Xft*hinting:            full

URxvt*inheritPixmap:    false
!URxvt*tintColor:       black
!URxvt*shading:         80
!URxvt*geometry:        80x17

!black
URxvt*color0:           #1d1e1f
URxvt*color8:           #424446
!red
URxvt*color1:           #9e6b71
URxvt*color9:           #b69094
!green
URxvt*color2:           #719e6b
URxvt*color10:          #94b690
!yellow
URxvt*color3:           #9e986c
URxvt*color11:          #b5b18f
!blue
URxvt*color4:           #6c8b9e
URxvt*color12:          #90a7b6
!magenta
URxvt*color5:           #986b9e
URxvt*color13:          #b290b6
!cyan
URxvt*color6:           #6b9e98
URxvt*color14:          #90b6b3
!white
URxvt*color7:           #b8baba
URxvt*color15:          #cdcfce


```Here's the custom MoC theme.
```
# Custom Theme No.8:
background               = default    default
frame                    = black    default    bold
window_title             = cyan    default    
directory                = yellow    default    
selected_directory       = white    default 
playlist                 = default    default    bold
selected_playlist        = red    default    bold
file                     = green    default       
selected_file            = red    default    bold
marked_file              = white    default      
marked_selected_file     = yellow    default    bold
info                     = default    default    bold
selected_info            = red    default    bold
marked_info              = white    default    
marked_selected_info     = yellow    default    bold
status                   = blue    default       
title                    = yellow  default    bold   
state                    = red    default   
current_time             = cyan    default
time_left                = magenta    default    
total_time               = black    default    bold   
time_total_frames        = black    default    bold
sound_parameters         = magenta    default    bold
legend                   = default    default
disabled                 = black    default    bold
enabled                  = blue    default    bold
empty_mixer_bar          = default    default
filled_mixer_bar         = default    default    reverse
empty_time_bar           = default    default
filled_time_bar          = default    default    reverse
entry                    = red    default
entry_title              = green    default
error                    = red    default    bold
message                  = yellow    default    bold
plist_time               = yellow    default    bold
```

### Post by c00lwaterz on 2010-11-08

---

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2010-11-08
> **c00lwaterz said:**
> Hi, this is nice.

I wonder how you do it dark in side panel and in the window. my window is look like this (in my attachment). 


I like the way you do it. pls help :P

Hi c00lwaterz,  
Sure, 
 First you have to be using "TESB/or "the empire strikes back" version of the theme. 
 If you installed the theme from the first download, 
before jurialmunkey updated the file with the new installer,
you should be able to find it in your theme preference window.
something like "A New Hope - TESB" . 

 Or, if you install it from the new installer, 
you can just choose "the empire strikes back" version to start with, so when the theme is applied, it will go directly to the dark version. 


 To change the background/window color..
go to "edit" menu, 
then "backgrounds and emblems"
[ATTACH]174957[/ATTACH]

in backgrounds and emblems, 
choose the "colors" 'tab'..
[ATTACH]174958[/ATTACH]

Then, 
 you can either choose one of the colors already there, 
or you can 'make' your own color, with the "add a new color" button @ bottom. 

 Once you have the color you want, in the color window,
you simply "Drag" it over into/onto your folder background. 
See the "Hope" color in mine? 
[ATTACH]174959[/ATTACH]

 You would just grab that, and drag it into the 'folder', 
and the background will change to that color. 

 hope that helps. <3

---

### Post by StrayVexel on 2010-11-10
> **gutterslob said:**
> Cheers

[[IMG]http://ompldr.org/tNjJmcg[/IMG]]("http://ompldr.org/vNjJmcg")

I've since tweaked the Xdef colours a tiny bit. Still pretty similar to the scrot your quoted.
I removed most of my app-related bits. What's here should be enough to get you the colour-scheme.
```
urxvt*font:             xft:terminus:pixelsize=8
urxvt*boldFont:         xft:terminus:pixelsize=8
urxvt*termName:         rxvt
urxvt*background:       #212629
urxvt*foreground:       #656e72
urxvt*scrollBar:        false
urxvt*matcher.button:   1
urxvt*cursorBlink:      true
urxvt*cursorColor:      #b1b6c8
urxvt*colorBD:          #857672

urxvt.transparent:      false
urxvt*allow_bold:       true

Xft*dpi:                96
Xft*antialias:          false
Xft*hinting:            full

URxvt*inheritPixmap:    false
!URxvt*tintColor:       black
!URxvt*shading:         80
!URxvt*geometry:        80x17

!black
URxvt*color0:           #1d1e1f
URxvt*color8:           #424446
!red
URxvt*color1:           #9e6b71
URxvt*color9:           #b69094
!green
URxvt*color2:           #719e6b
URxvt*color10:          #94b690
!yellow

### Post by roguebuck on 2010-11-11
why thank you. im running 10.10, tweaked avant to look a little like a launcher bar. 
that is one of the nicest backgrounds ive seen, and it comes with 10.10!, but here is a linky to it:

[[IMG]http://lh3.ggpht.com/_FJH0hYZmVtc/THbTmgG-A_I/AAAAAAAAJcY/ouupbpJDUO4/Bubbles_by_JanneM[4]_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800[/IMG]]("http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_QkWfBvmBstU/TKDFo7hMwlI/AAAAAAAAAfc/f7pQeTv7LEQ/s1600/Ubuntu+10.10+Wallpapers+(16).jpg")

my conky.conf:
```
# Use Xft?
use_xft yes
xftfont Trebuchet MS:size=8
xftalpha 0.8
text_buffer_size 1024

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 3

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
    own_window no
    own_window_transparent no
    own_window_type desktop
    own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 180 0

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 10

# border margins
border_margin 5

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
own_window_colour white

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment top_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 35
gap_y 65

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer none

TEXT
SYSTEM ${hr 2}
${alignc}Ubuntu 10.10-Maverick
${alignc}${kernel}
uid:$alignr$nodename
extIP:${alignr}${execi 3600 wget -O - http://whatismyip.org/ | tail}
cpu:${alignr}${cpu cpu}% ${cpubar 8,60 cpu}
uptime: ${alignr}${uptime}

DATE ${hr 2}

${alignc 35}${font Trebuchet MS:size=26}${time %H:%M}${font}
${alignc}${time %a %d %b %Y}


RESOURCES ${hr 2}
CPU1 $alignr ${cpu cpu1}%
$alignr${cpugraph cpu1 20,180 789E2D A7CC5C}
CPU2 $alignr ${cpu cpu2}%
$alignr${cpugraph cpu2 20,180 789E2D A7CC5C}
RAM$alignr $memperc%
${alignr}${membar 8,180 789E2D A7CC5C}

$processes processes $alignr ($running_processes running)${font}
${hr 2}
$alignr PID    CPU
${top name 1} $alignr ${top pid 1} ${top cpu 1}
${top name 2} $alignr ${top pid 2} ${top cpu 2}
${top name 3} $alignr ${top pid 3} ${top cpu 3}
${top name 4} $alignr ${top pid 4} ${top cpu 4}

HD ${hr 2}
/home $alignr ${fs_free_perc /}% 
$alignr${fs_used /} / ${fs_size /} ${fs_bar 8,60 /}
/mnt/MEDIA $alignr ${fs_free_perc /mnt/MEDIA}%
$alignr${fs_used /mnt/MEDIA} / ${fs_size /mnt/MEDIA} ${fs_bar 8,60 /mnt/MEDIA}
/mnt/MEDIA2 $alignr ${fs_free_perc /mnt/MEDIA2}%
$alignr${fs_used /mnt/MEDIA2} / ${fs_size /mnt/MEDIA2} ${fs_bar 8,60 /mnt/MEDIA2}
/mnt/MEDIA3 $alignr ${fs_free_perc /mnt/MEDIA3}%
$alignr${fs_used /mnt/MEDIA3} / ${fs_size /mnt/MEDIA3} ${fs_bar 8,60 /mnt/MEDIA3}
swap $alignr $swapperc% 
$alignr$swap / $swapmax ${swapbar 8,60}

NETWORK ${hr 2}${if_existing /proc/net/route wlan0}
up: ${upspeed wlan0} kb/s ${alignr}${upspeedgraph wlan0 8,60 789E2D A7CC5C}
down: ${downspeed wlan0} kb/s ${alignr}${downspeedgraph wlan0 8,60 789E2D A7CC5C}
upload: ${alignr}${totalup wlan0}
download: ${alignr}${totaldown wlan0}
signal: ${wireless_link_qual wlan0}% ${alignr}${wireless_link_bar 8,60 wlan0}${else}
${if_existing /proc/net/route eth0}
up: ${upspeed eth0} kb/s ${alignr}${upspeedgraph eth0 8,60 789E2D A7CC5C}
down: ${downspeed eth0} kb/s ${alignr}${downspeedgraph eth0 8,60 789E2D A7CC5C}
upload: ${alignr}${totalup eth0}
download: ${alignr}${totaldown eth0}${endif}${else}
${if_existing /proc/net/route eth1}
up: ${upspeed eth1} kb/s ${alignr}${upspeedgraph eth1 8,60 789E2D A7CC5C}
down: ${downspeed eth1} kb/s ${alignr}${downspeedgraph eth1 8,60 789E2D A7CC5C}
upload: ${alignr}${totalup eth1}
download: ${alignr}${totaldown eth1}${endif}${else}${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=14}4${font}   Network Unavailable${endif}

WEATHER ${hr 2}
${if_existing /proc/net/route wlan0}
${voffset -8}${alignr 56}${font ConkyWeather:style=Bold:size=40}${execi 600 conkyForecast --location=USOR0076 --datatype=WF}${font}
${voffset -52}${font Weather:size=40}${font}   ${voffset -38}${font Trebuchet MS:size=26}${execi 600 conkyForecast --imperial --location=USOR0076 --datatype=HT}${font}

```

it took me a while to figure out the weather script, but i finally got it to work using this how-to (says it only goes up to karmic, but it worked fine in maverick just sub in 'maverick' for 'karmic' everywhere)

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=869328]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=869328")

> Hi Rassa,,

Looks good!
 Nice job! :D

Ok, for the indicator applet.. 
( we are talking about your "volume and email/messaging" indicators right?)

To change that to be side by side, rather than one on top of the other.. 

 simply right click the applet, 
go to "preferences" and change "number of rows" from 2 to 1.
and check "enable applet icon mode" (or something like that) lol

To add the 'wifi'/network' icon to AWN, 
you first have to remove it from the top/main panel . 

 So, on the top panel, right click on the network indicator applet, choose to "remove from panel", and when that is removed,
open your AWN preferences, 
go into "Applets" , and add the "Notification area" to your AWN dock/panel. [ATTACH]175322[/ATTACH]

> Thanks again rassa

 No problem my friend,
 anytime. :)
 <3

### Post by slackthumbz on 2010-11-11
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> 
The top panel, needs to be removed with a command.
 the command is 
```
sudo apt-get remove gnome-panel
```

 I have not removed my top panel (now on the bottom, and hidden)
simply because I am fine with it on autohide [for now] . lol
but eventually i will remove it I think. 


WOAH THERE!! You don't need to uninstall gnome-panel to disable it! Open up gconf-editor, go to Desktop->Gnome->Session->required_components and simply remove gnome-panel there (I replaced it with avant-window-navigator). Then log out and log back in again. Simples!

See the attached screenie :)

---

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-11
++

You can also use Ubuntu Tweak's session control option to change what displays the panel. Under session-control change "panel" from *gnome-panel* to *avant-window-navigator* and hit apply. :D

I find this to be the simplest and most easily revertible way of removing the panel (I assume Ubuntu Tweak just changes the gconf key, but I find it easier as I don't have to navigate gconf's registry like structure!).

---

 The bottom panel, you can just right click and choose "delete/remove this panel"

The top panel, needs to be removed with a command.
 the command is 
```
sudo apt-get remove gnome-panel
```

 I have not removed my top panel (now on the bottom, and hidden)
simply because I am fine with it on autohide [for now] . lol

you first have to remove it from the top/main panel . 

 So, on the top panel, right click on the network indicator applet, choose to "remove from panel", and when that is removed,
open your AWN preferences, 
go into "Applets" , and add the "Notification area" to your AWN dock/panel. [ATTACH]175322[/ATTACH]

Either:

Install something like gmrun and reconfigure alt-f2 to run it.

or

Install guake/yakuake drop down terminal, always useful in emergencies.

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-11
> **xircon said:**
> Install something like gmrun and reconfigure alt-f2 to run it.

++ gmrun !!! Its by far my favourite.. Its replaced my ALT+F2 permanently. Can't live without its TAB entry completion. 

Other Options -->
[LIST]
[*]Create a shortcut/launcher on the desktop for AWN
[*]Use a right-click openbox style deskmenu like compiz-deskmenu
[*]Use a launcher program such as ["The Launcher"]("http://www.alte.ru/thelauncher/") and bind it to a key combo
[*]Create a key-binding that launches the terminal (I use ALT+F1). I used to use tilda as a drop down terminal but I found it impractical compared to simply firing up a terminal as a window.
[*]Gnome-do or Kupfer
[*]Use Cardapio in stand-alone mode.
[/LIST]

 Ok, The network manager/indicator, 
is a little bit tricker to remove.. 
not in steps, only that you have to click on the exact perfect place. 

 Depending on what theme youre using,
it can be hard (or impossible) to see the little "line" that is next to the network manager indicator. 

 If I recall, it is to the left of the "icons"..
and if you click to far to the left or the right.. 
it will not give the option to remove. 
It has to be precise. 

 and it can be a pain to get. lol


The wifi icon, is the same (and/or in the same place as the 'wired' connection icon when connected via ethernet. 

 So if your using wifi, the wifi icon will be visible,
 and if you are plugged into ethernet, the wifi icon will disappear and the 'wired' icon will show in its place. 

 to the left of that icon, should be a tiny line, that looks like 3 "dashes" one on top of the other. 
like this,  only closer together. 
-
-
-

 that is what you must right click to bring up the "remove" option.

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-12
> **Tigerclawz said:**
> This has probably been asked a thousand times, so in that regard, I appologize, however:

Can someone please tell me how to, or post a link on creating these transparent window backgrounds and the curvy-colour-change panel thing?

Much appreciated, in advance.

The panel is Avant-Window-Navigator (AWN for short) Lucido style: [AWN Lucido Install Instructions]("http://www.webupd8.org/2010/06/awn-lucido-gets-its-own-ppa.html")

Rasa had a post a page or two ago about setting up AWN.

For themes with transparent window borders, you need Emerald. Emerald requires Compiz compositing to run. 
```
sudo apt-get install emerald libemeraldengine0
```

*To install [emerald themes], go to: System > Preferences > Emerald Theme Manager and click the "Import" button and select the themes you want. To make your windows use Emerald, go to System > Preferences > CompizConfig Settings Manager and enable "Window Decoration", then click it and under "Command", enter:*
```
emerald --replace
```

Then hit ALT+F2 to get a run dialog and type the "emerald --replace" command there as well and hit enter. 

The "emerald --replace" command switches from Metacity to Emerald decorations. "gtk-window-decorator --replace" switches back to metacity. (Italics from [WebUpd8]("http://www.webupd8.org/2009/03/ubuntu-install-themes-emerald-compiz.html"))

My theme: [Divergence IV - A New Hope]("http://jurialmunkey.deviantart.com/art/Divergence-IV-quot-A-New-Hope-quot-183377193") uses glassy emerald borders with a style similar to Lucido AWN and has been quite popular. 

For actual transparent windows, you need the Murrine RGBA module or you can use compiz opacity settings.

and my tint2rc:

```

# Tint2 config file
# Generated by tintwizard (http://code.google.com/p/tintwizard/)
# For information on manually configuring tint2 see http://code.google.com/p/tint2/wiki/Configure

# To use this as default tint2 config: save as $HOME/.config/tint2/tint2rc

# Background definitions
# ID 1
rounded = 2
border_width = 1
background_color = #000000 0
border_color = #000000 100

# ID 2
rounded = 2
border_width = 1
background_color = #000000 78
border_color = #FFFFFF 100

# ID 3
rounded = 3
border_width = 1
background_color = #000000 78
border_color = #E4D07D 100

# Panel
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = bottom center horizontal
panel_size = 94% 25
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 7 0 7
panel_dock = 0
wm_menu = 1
panel_layer = top
panel_background_id = 0

# Panel Autohide
autohide = 0
autohide_show_timeout = 0.3
autohide_hide_timeout = 2
autohide_height = 2
strut_policy = follow_size

# Taskbar
taskbar_mode = single_desktop
taskbar_padding = 0 0 10
taskbar_background_id = 0
taskbar_active_background_id = 0

# Tasks
urgent_nb_of_blink = 8
task_icon = 1
task_text = 1
task_centered = 1
task_maximum_size = 100 0
task_padding = 0 1
task_background_id = 1
task_active_background_id = 2
task_urgent_background_id = 2
task_iconified_background_id = 1

# Task Icons
task_icon_asb = 80 0 0
task_active_icon_asb = 100 0 0
task_urgent_icon_asb = 100 0 0
task_iconified_icon_asb = 80 0 0

# Fonts
task_font = Diavlo Medium 9
task_font_color = #000000 100
task_active_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
task_urgent_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
task_iconified_font_color = #000000 100
font_shadow = 0

# System Tray
systray = 1
systray_padding = 2 4 2
systray_sort = ascending
systray_background_id = 3
systray_icon_size = 16
systray_icon_asb = 100 0 0

# Clock
time1_format = %I:%M %p
time1_font = sans 8
time2_format = %A %d %B
time2_font = sans 6
clock_font_color = #FFFFFF 80
clock_padding = 2 0
clock_background_id = 3

# Tooltips
tooltip = 0
tooltip_padding = 2 2
tooltip_show_timeout = 0.7
tooltip_hide_timeout = 0.3
tooltip_background_id = 1
tooltip_font = sans 10
tooltip_font_color = #000000 80

# Mouse
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

# Battery
battery = 0
battery_low_status = 10
battery_low_cmd = notify-send "battery low"
battery_hide = 98
bat1_font = sans 8
bat2_font = sans 6
battery_font_color = #FFFFFF 72
battery_padding = 1 0
battery_background_id = 0

# End of config

```

Now,

 Say, theoretically.. 
that all of the sudden AWN decided to 'crash' or something.. 
and one had to "quit" it. 

 How would one go about starting it back up again,
if the main panel is gone, and AWN is not running? 
ie... no way to get into a 'main menu'? 

 I have had to 'quit' AWN only once or twice, 
but to start it back up I just went into the 'top panel' menu, and opened 'AWN'. 

but with top panel no longer in use,
how would one go about re-starting AWN, with no menu?

By disabling gnome-panel you also lose gnomes default "Run Application" dialog because it's part of the panel app. To compensate for this install grun
```
sudo apt-get install grun
```
Go to Preferences->Keyboard Shortcuts and add a shortcut for grun (I use ctrl+F2) that way if AWN crashes you can just hit Ctrl+F2 (in my case) and type in avant-window-navigator to restart the application.

---

See screenshot :) Once that's done under "Shortcut" it'll say 'disabled'. Click on the word 'disabled' and it'll say 'New shortcut' then press the key combination you want to use. For example in my set up I pressed Ctrl+F2.

Hope that helps :)

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2010-11-12
> **slackthumbz said:**
> By disabling gnome-panel you also lose gnomes default "Run Application" dialog because it's part of the panel app. To compensate for this install grun
```
sudo apt-get install grun
```
Go to Preferences->Keyboard Shortcuts and add a shortcut for grun (I use ctrl+F2) that way if AWN crashes you can just hit Ctrl+F2 (in my case) and type in avant-window-navigator to restart the application.

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-12
> **koleoptero said:**
> If one could add glow on the borders in a gtk theme (widget borders) then it would fit quite well I believe. I don't think it's possible though unfortunately :/

With the latest murrine engine it is possible to define both the shade and colour of widget borders using *border_colors {#HEX, #HEX}* and *border_shades {1.0, 1.0}*. By being inventive with border shades and lightborders, you can sort of achieve a glow effect. Or there are always pixmap themes....

Another idea would be to change the window shadows to a glow like in KDE (change from black shadows to blue or white shadows). That gives a sense of glowing windows.

---

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-13
> **Rasa1111 said:**

assign something like ctrl A W N , or alt A W N to open AWN. 
or am i wrong? 
that would be cool. lol  :P

I think its possible to do but causes way too many problems. It means that nothing can be assigned to Alt+A, Alt+W & Alt+N otherwise whatever is assigned to Alt+A will get called first (so it may as well be assigned to Alt+A rather than Alt+AWN). Also, its really difficult to hit the N with the left hand... and you generally want keyboard shortcuts on the left so your right hand doesn't have to leave the mouse.

The main icon theme I use is Azenis Icons, from gnome-look.org:
[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Azenis+Icons?content=107544](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Azenis+Icons?content=107544)

[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Azenis?content=106608](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Azenis?content=106608) 

The Cairo Dock icons are custom icons I made using the Gallifrey Brushes by PurpleRhino from Deviant art. I haven't uploaded them, as I need to do some more work, but once I am done I'll add them to gnome-look as well.

### Post by Firepower-EX on 2010-11-14
> **Helkaluin said:**
> Is that tint2? Care to share your config?

Sure. I created it using tint2conf.

```
# ID 1
rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #B7B7B7 40
border_color = #FFFFFF 84

# ID 2
rounded = 2
border_width = 0
background_color = #57A5E9 60
border_color = #FFFFFF 40

# ID 3
rounded = 3
border_width = 0
background_color = #C5C5C5 40
border_color = #FFFFFF 60

# Panel
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = bottom center horizontal
panel_size = 100% 22
panel_margin = 2 6
panel_padding = 2 0 5
panel_dock = 0
wm_menu = 1
panel_layer = top
panel_background_id = 1

# Panel Autohide
autohide = 0
autohide_show_timeout = 0.3
autohide_hide_timeout = 2
autohide_height = 2
strut_policy = follow_size

# Taskbar
taskbar_mode = single_desktop
taskbar_padding = 2 3 2
taskbar_background_id = 0
taskbar_active_background_id = 0

# Tasks
urgent_nb_of_blink = 8
task_icon = 0
task_text = 1
task_centered = 1
task_maximum_size = 150 35
task_padding = 6 5
task_background_id = 0
task_active_background_id = 2
task_urgent_background_id = 2
task_iconified_background_id = 0

# Task Icons
task_icon_asb = 70 0 0
task_active_icon_asb = 100 0 0
task_urgent_icon_asb = 100 0 0
task_iconified_icon_asb = 70 0 0

# Fonts
task_font = Aller Bold 8
task_font_color = #D2D2D2 62
task_active_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
task_urgent_font_color = #FFFFFF 80
task_iconified_font_color = #D0D0D0 60
font_shadow = 0

# System Tray
systray = 1
systray_padding = 3 0 9
systray_sort = ascending
systray_background_id = 0
systray_icon_size = 16
systray_icon_asb = 85 -100 15

# Clock
time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = Aller Bold 9
clock_font_color = #FFFFFF 80
clock_tooltip = %a %d %b
clock_padding = 0 0
clock_background_id = 0

# Tooltips
tooltip = 1
tooltip_padding = 2 2
tooltip_show_timeout = 0.7
tooltip_hide_timeout = 0.3
tooltip_background_id = 1
tooltip_font = Aller 9
tooltip_font_color = #FFFFFF 100

# Mouse
mouse_middle = shade
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

# Battery
battery = 0
battery_low_status = 10
battery_low_cmd = notify-send "battery low"
battery_hide = 98
bat1_font = sans 8
bat2_font = sans 6
battery_font_color = #FFFFFF 60
battery_padding = 1 0
battery_background_id = 0

```

### Post by a-user on 2010-11-15
[@c00lwaterz]("http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=452948"):
look here:
[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/RGBA+Gtk%2B+module?content=100556]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/RGBA+Gtk%2B+module?content=100556")

this gives you a ppa with the gtk2-module-rgba modul.
now the point is, that this modul produces several problems with nautilus. this is because nautilus is also painting your desktop. the result is that you won't see your desktop image.
that's why there is also a nautilius verison in the ppa. this one has been modified to function proper with this modul.

so add this ppa and install the above modul. then make an upgrade so that nautilus gets updatet. for the rest read the infos in my link above.

now one more thing:
the modul from above has a debugin line
"printf ("\nprogname=%s; RGBA=on\n",progname);"

you will find the source code of the modul on the same page as first download link. get it and remove that line. compile it as explained and subsitute the librgba.so from the ppa with your self compiled one (edited this).

the reason is, that this will print a line of text with every programm you start that gets this modul applied. e.g. if you use conky and run a python script within, than you will see the output of the rgba modul in conky displayed. that's why you have to remove it.

p.s. don't remember to read the instructio on the gnome-look link.

---

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-16
> **Viva said:**
> I agree that options are limited with tabs. Pixmaps are an alternative though, as you said. You can use pixmap for the notebook part only, can't you?

> **Islington said:**
> pixmaps are generally more trouble than they are worth imho. no documentation+nonstandard behavior means that a themer tends to spend way more time on it.
^^^ THIS x 100. Pixmaps are a nightmare. SkiesofAzel is probably one of the best and most professional pixmap themers, and Orta is posing a number of real difficulties from use of pixmaps. If everything was just GTK or QT and didn't use weird implementations of widgets then we'd all be sweet. But that just isn't the nature of Linux in general, and to do so would limit our freedom - which is by far our greatest asset. Its also important to simplify and avoid using to many different theme engines. Evolution's use of Bonobo and weird GTK implementations has been a nightmare for theme makers - and this is a stock app for Ubuntu....

> **The Real Dave said:**
> It was about time for a change. I'd been with my last setup for months >.<

[[img]http://linuxexpresso.files.wordpress.com/2010/07/21-jul-2010-system64.png?w=150&h=120[/img]]("http://linuxexpresso.files.wordpress.com/2010/07/21-jul-2010-system64.png")

Also, love your conky.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-11-20
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> Anyone know how I can 'dock' those 4 desktop icons at the bottom, right where they are. somehow? lol

Add another AWN dock from its preferences, set its style to "None", remove all the applets it might have and add the simple launcher applet, then drag and drop there those 3 launchers. Set it to Autohide and Keep Below.

### Post by Islington on 2010-11-20
> **DJ_Peng said:**
> Thanks for posting the link but I have to be an idiot. How do I install them? I saw how to import the colors although I don't see the name in my color theme list but I have no idea how to import the Qt style.

Yep, I'm a dummy today, evidenced by the fact that while I was chopping onions for chili this am I sliced off a but of the side of my thumb. Luckily as soon as I felt the slice I moved my hand over the sink so I didn't flavor the onions but I now have a trio of band-aids on my thumb to help soak up quite a bit of blood. *D'oh!*

mmm... chilli, now there is a splendid idea for lunch.

you install the colors directly over the ghns button in syssettings> applicationappearance> colors> getnewschemes> install G. if that doesn't work download the file manually and import it manually.

save the .qtcurve file on your desktop(file>save as). go to syssettings> applicationappearance> style> widgetstyle: qtcurve> click the configure button> click the import button in the dialog that shows up> import your saved file.

:D

The launchers would change at both because you used the launcher/taskmanager applet, not the simple launcher applet. There are two. Use the other ;) It will have launchers but won't manage the applications themselves.

You can change the settings for each dock seperately. You can't change the theme though, that stays the same. If you set it to none though then it'll look the same no matter what theme you use, right? :P

After that when you want to change the options for any specific dock, right-click on it and select "dock preferences" there, don't use the preferences applet.

What I suggested is doable with the version from the ppa, I don't know about the version that's in the repos.

---

### Post by CoffeeCoder on 2010-11-23
I've tweaked my desktop around a bit. Finally was able to since I got internet access back (was without it for 11 days!). :P

**Theme:** Lucidity Dark
**Icon Set:** Faenza Dark
**Dock:** Awn
**Dock Theme: **Dust Theme

I also modified the top panel to operate a little more like Windows (just what I'm used to). I put the Window List there, used the GNOME Main Menu, and made sure the windows combine in the list when I'm running multiple instances of the same application. It's just handier and allows more real estate for other applications. :)

The background is the space slideshow that comes default with 10.10. I quite like it. :D

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-11-24
> **c00lwaterz said:**
> i don't really know what is this. i heard this but i don't have idea about crunchbang linux. how this works? is this same as ubuntu? im really noobs:DHeh. The screenshot is misleading. What you see on screen is a standard Debian netinstall running ScrotWM (window manager) with a cli feedreader, irc client and browser, and looks nothing like CrunchBang Linux does. The reason you see all the Crunchbang related stuff is because I posted that screenie in the Crunchbang forums prior to posting here.

CrunchBang is actually quite a nice distro. It comes in 2 flavours, OpenBox and Xfce. The Xfce version is probably a bit more beginner-friendly, though I personally prefer Openbox or other *box types window managers compared to full-on desktop environments. They just give me a tad more control and tend to not get in my way as much. I don't actually use Crunchbang right now, but nearly all my Openbox setups on various rigs are sort of Crunchbang-inspired in one-way or another, mostly with regards to app choice and some configs.

### Post by Spice Weasel on 2010-11-24
Crux window borders... :D That takes me back.

I've been working on my DE a fair bit, created a few scripts to make it easier to use, reduced memory usage by around 15MB (it used to use 50MB), cleaned out A LOT of code and added a couple flashy features. For example, if I am stuck without a keyboard and want to run a script or program that is not on the menu, I can draw its name on the desktop and it will run. The sidebar and taskbar scroll in and hide themselves in one click, so they don't waste that much screen space.

I turned transparency off and switched to a white theme because it was getting on my nerves... And eyes.

[[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/J4n3vl.jpg[/IMG]]("http://imgur.com/J4n3v.png")

### Post by hhh on 2010-11-24
> **koleoptero said:**
> **@gutterslob:** I wouldn't call the xfce version of #! a full blown DE, it misses a lot of stuff, like the panel to say the least. LOL
It is a full blown DE, it's just been tweaked to mimic #!'s Openbox setup. The Xfce panel is turned off and replaced by tint2, but you can disable or remove tint2 and start up xfce4-panel with no problems. The only other changes I can think of are that desktop icons are disabled and can be enabled via Settings>Desktop>Icons>Appearance>Icon Type, and that toolbars in apps are set to text only which can be changed via Settings>Appearance>Settings>Toolbar Style.

To those who liked the AT-AT wallpaper, cool. That shot is from this Flickr group which has some incredibly cool other shots which you need to sign in to download (check out the Death Star over downtown San Fran and the Star Destroyer over the Bay Bridge!)...
[http://www.flickr.com/photos/hornage/sets/72157621885493550/detail/](http://www.flickr.com/photos/hornage/sets/72157621885493550/detail/)

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-11-30
> **Islington said:**
> looks good, although it makes me wonder if you will run into some problems from firefox/office with an inverted dark color in the entryfields? Or maybe that has been solved now.

also another point coming to mind is that the white text color may be too white. I personally find a lighter gray easier to use against a dark background :)

anyways looks really good.

Thanks :D

Yeah, I'm pretty sure I'm setting my self up for a ton of issues using dark entryboxes. There is probably going to be a lot of "per app" styling. I'm thinking I'll probably just make a Firefox theme. Office I might have to just use light entryboxes, but Office never looks right with any theme, so as long as its functional (i.e. all widget text is readable) I'm not too concerned. But yeah, due to all the per app styling I'll have to do, I can't imagine its going to be the fastest theme. I'm doing it more as a proof of concept than anything else though.

I think I will use a slightly darker font colour in the end. At the moment I'm just trying to get the dark style for the Notebook/Tab content to work properly and consistently. I pretty much had to make a separate dark theme for every widget to use inside the content of Tabs.

It might take some time to finish it, but so far its coming along so much better than I expected :D
